  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_80037860" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80037860" />
    <a title="Amanda Patterson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3010986-amanda-patterson"><img alt="Amanda Patterson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510113725p2/3010986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80037860?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Patterson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Patterson" href="/user/show/3010986-amanda-patterson">Amanda Patterson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80037860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4697523046088197070">Kisscut reminded me of the heady first novels written by Patricia Cornwell. I hate to tear down my idols but I believe that Slaughter may be better than all the rest. As I’m writing this review, I’ve ordered a copy of her first novel, Blindsighted.<br/><br/>Sara Linton, small town paediatrician and coroner, is a worthy serial heroine. Sara is out on a date with her ex-husband, Jeffrey Tolliver. He is also the local police chief. On his way to meet Sara, he is forced to kill a girl who is threatening other</span>
  <span id="freeText4697523046088197070" style="display:none">Kisscut reminded me of the heady first novels written by Patricia Cornwell. I hate to tear down my idols but I believe that Slaughter may be better than all the rest. As I’m writing this review, I’ve ordered a copy of her first novel, Blindsighted.<br /><br />Sara Linton, small town paediatrician and coroner, is a worthy serial heroine. Sara is out on a date with her ex-husband, Jeffrey Tolliver. He is also the local police chief. On his way to meet Sara, he is forced to kill a girl who is threatening other residents with a gun.<br /><br />A horrific journey into the heart of Grant County begins. A terrifying ring of paedophilia is uncovered. Appearances are deceptive and no one really knows anyone, do they? Jeffrey, Sara and Detective Lena Adams are forced to confront the evil in their own backyard. The brilliance of this book is that the rural normalcy of small town USA is a perfect backdrop in which to set this thriller.<br /><br />Slaughter’s characterisation is superb. Sara yearns for her ex-husband, who cheated on her. Jeffrey yearns for Sara. We discover that Sara is unable to have children. Detective Lena Adams is still recovering from the horrors she endured in Blindsighted. She is still suicidal, more a frightened girl than tough female cop and yet you root for her.<br /><br />The characters and storyline of Kisscut by Karin Slaughter will remain in your mind days after you’ve stopped reading. Slaughter is one of those authors who constantly remind me that we as readers should lobby for ‘thrillers’ to be considered for ‘literary’ prizes. Other authors who fit the bill are Jeffrey Deaver, Ian Rankin and Michael Connelly.<br /><br />If you are a fan of forensic crime thrillers, read this book. If you are a reader who enjoys a good story and good characters, read this book. I don’t think we’ve seen the best of Karin Slaughter yet.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4697523046088197070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4m4domrn0EcKjPBJLIshuwN1iTWsEnqq07F4vigQlgTUlzselWLW2h/Yx0lqzNM32wyWbX7SLbEV1fsvpeg0lQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BKi4hi52Yud+OTksjhvcXJ4tfV25xj785pOj0rRgrxoyUZ460fNkemttDizIXC7QRlRiBWsGaecg9yBDOZgNiw==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer7991653892313215401">Karin Slaughter is one of the world’s most popular and acclaimed storytellers. Published in 120 countries with more than 35 million copies sold across the globe, her nineteen novels include the Grant County and Will Trent books, as well as the Edgar-nominated COP TOWN and the instant NEW YORK TIMES bestselling novels PRETTY GIRLS, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and PIECES OF HER. Her most recent book, THE LAS</span>
  <span id="freeText7991653892313215401" style="display:none">Karin Slaughter is one of the world’s most popular and acclaimed storytellers. Published in 120 countries with more than 35 million copies sold across the globe, her nineteen novels include the Grant County and Will Trent books, as well as the Edgar-nominated COP TOWN and the instant NEW YORK TIMES bestselling novels PRETTY GIRLS, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and PIECES OF HER. Her most recent book, THE LAST WIDOW, features Sara Linton and Will Trent. Slaughter is the founder of the Save the Libraries project—a nonprofit organization established to support libraries and library programming. A native of Georgia, Karin Slaughter lives in Atlanta. Her standalone novels PIECES OF HER, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and COP TOWN are in development for film and television.<br /><br /><br /><b>Facebook:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://Facebook.com/AuthorKarinSlaughter">Facebook.com/AuthorKarinSlaughter</a> <br /><br /><b>Website</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.karinslaughter.com/">http://www.karinslaughter.com/</a><br /><br /><b>Instagram</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/karinslaughterauthor/">https://www.instagram.com/karinslaugh...</a><br /></span>

      $('bookCover_21720').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
